class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg 1.5x, north-west</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Gibraltar</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/d\xca\x92/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">d\xca\x92</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x99r/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">\xc9\x99r</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">jih-<span style="font-size:90%">BRAWL</span>-t\xc9\x99r</i></a>, <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[xi\xce\xb2\xc9\xbeal\xcb\x88ta\xc9\xbe]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> located at the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It has an area of 6.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2.6&#160;sq&#160;mi) and is <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar%E2%80%93Spain_border" title="Gibraltar\xe2\x80\x93Spain border">bordered to the north</a> by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. The landscape is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a> at the foot of which is a densely populated town area, home to over 32,000 people, primarily <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarians" title="Gibraltarians">Gibraltarians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1704, Anglo-Dutch forces <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">captured Gibraltar</a> from Spain during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> claim to the Spanish throne. The territory was ceded to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> in perpetuity under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> in 1713. During the Napoleonic Wars and World War II it was an important base for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> as it controlled the entrance and exit to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, which is only 14.3&#160;km (8.9&#160;mi) wide at this naval <a href="/wiki/Choke_point" title="Choke point">choke point</a>. It remains strategically important, with half the world\'s seaborne trade passing through the strait.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Today Gibraltar\'s economy is based largely on tourism, online gambling, financial services and <a href="/wiki/Bunkering" title="Bunkering">bunkering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maec_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maec-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sovereignty of Gibraltar is a point of contention in <a href="/wiki/Spain%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Spain\xe2\x80\x93United Kingdom relations">Anglo-Spanish relations</a> because Spain asserts <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" class="mw-redirect" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">a claim to the territory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maec_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maec-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Gibraltarians rejected proposals for Spanish sovereignty in a <a href="/wiki/1967_Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum" title="1967 Gibraltar sovereignty referendum">1967 referendum</a> and, in a <a href="/wiki/2002_Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum" title="2002 Gibraltar sovereignty referendum">2002 referendum</a>, the idea of shared sovereignty was also rejected.\n</p><p>On 31 January 2020, the UK and Gibraltar <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">left the European Union</a>. In December 2020, the UK and Spain agreed in principle to a basis  on which the UK and the EU might negotiate terms for Gibraltar to participate in aspects of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GibStatement_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GibStatement-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a history</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Middle_Ages"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Middle Ages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 class="toctext">Governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Environment</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Ethnic_groups"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ethnic groups</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Health_care"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Health care</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Cultural_references"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Cultural references</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Communications"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Communications</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Road"><span class="tocnumber">13.1</span> <span class="toctext">Road</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Air"><span class="tocnumber">13.2</span> <span class="toctext">Air</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Sea"><span class="tocnumber">13.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sea</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Rail"><span class="tocnumber">13.4</span> <span class="toctext">Rail</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Water_supply_and_sanitation"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Water supply and sanitation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Police"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Police</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Armed_forces"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Armed forces</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Twin_towns_and_sister_cities"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Twin towns and sister cities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Freedom_of_the_City"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">Freedom of the City</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#People"><span class="tocnumber">18.1</span> <span class="toctext">People</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Military_units"><span class="tocnumber">18.2</span> <span class="toctext">Military units</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Organisations_and_groups"><span class="tocnumber">18.3</span> <span class="toctext">Organisations and groups</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">20</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">21</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">22</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">23</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>\n<p>The name is derived from <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xac\xd8\xa8\xd9\x84 \xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x82</span>&#8206;, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Jabal \xe1\xb9\xac\xc4\x81riq</i>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a>&#8201;</small>&#39;Mount of Tariq&#39; (named after the 8th century Moorish military leader <a href="/wiki/Tariq_ibn_Ziyad" title="Tariq ibn Ziyad">Tariq ibn Ziyad</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-WattCachia2007_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WattCachia2007-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> That continues to be its name in Arabic. It has also been suggested that the name is a contraction of <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xac\xd8\xa8\xd9\x84 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82</span>&#8206;, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">jabal `al\xc4\x81 a\xe1\xb9\xad-\xe1\xb9\xadar\xc4\xabq</i>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a>&#8201;</small>&#39;mount on the way [from Africa to Iberia]&#39;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Gibraltar" title="History of Gibraltar">History of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/170px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/255px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/340px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2136" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the northern face of the <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Castle" title="Moorish Castle">Moorish Castle</a>\'s Tower of Homage</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_ancient_history">Prehistory and ancient history</span></h3>\n<p>Evidence of <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> habitation in Gibraltar from around 50,000 years ago has been discovered at <a href="/wiki/Gorham%27s_Cave" title="Gorham&#39;s Cave">Gorham\'s Cave</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The caves of Gibraltar continued to be used by <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" class="mw-redirect" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> after the final extinction of the Neanderthals. Stone tools, ancient hearths and animal bones dating from around 40,000 years ago to about 5,000 years ago have been found in deposits left in Gorham\'s Cave.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Numerous potsherds dating from the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period have been found in Gibraltar\'s caves, mostly of types typical of the <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Iberia" title="Prehistoric Iberia">Almerian culture</a> found elsewhere in Andalusia, especially around the town of <a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almer\xc3\xada">Almer\xc3\xada</a>, from which it takes its name.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> There is little evidence of habitation in the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> when people had largely stopped living in caves.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During ancient times, Gibraltar was regarded by the peoples of the Mediterranean as a place of religious and symbolic importance. The <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> were present for several centuries since around 950 BC, apparently using Gorham\'s Cave as a shrine to the <i><a href="/wiki/Genius_loci" title="Genius loci">genius loci</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> as did the <a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> after them. Gibraltar was known as <i><a href="/wiki/Mons_Calpe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mons Calpe">Mons Calpe</a></i>, a name perhaps of Phoenician origin.<sup id="cite_ref-Hills-13_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hills-13-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <i>Mons Calpe</i> was considered by the ancient Greeks and Romans as one of the <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">Pillars of Hercules</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> legend of the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> by <a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">Heracles</a>. There is no known archaeological evidence of permanent settlements from the ancient period.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> They settled at the head of the bay in what is today known as the <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Gibraltar" title="Campo de Gibraltar"><i>Campo</i> (hinterland) of Gibraltar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson22_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson22-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The town of <a href="/wiki/Carteia" title="Carteia">Carteia</a>, near the location of the modern Spanish town of <a href="/wiki/San_Roque,_C%C3%A1diz" class="mw-redirect" title="San Roque, C\xc3\xa1diz">San Roque</a>, was founded by the Phoenicians around 950 BC on the site of an early settlement of the native <a href="/wiki/Turdetani" title="Turdetani">Turdetani</a> people.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span></h3>\n<p>After the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>, Gibraltar came briefly under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, who crossed into Africa at the invitation of <a href="/wiki/Bonifacius" title="Bonifacius">Boniface</a>, the Count (or commander) of the territory.\n</p><p>The area later formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> for almost 300 years, from 414 until 711 AD.\n</p><p>Following a raid in 710, a predominantly Berber army under the command of <a href="/wiki/Tariq_ibn_Ziyad" title="Tariq ibn Ziyad">Tariq ibn Ziyad</a> crossed from North Africa in April 711 and landed somewhere in the vicinity of Gibraltar (though most likely not in the bay or at the Rock itself).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson21\xe2\x80\x935_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson21\xe2\x80\x935-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Tariq\'s expedition led to the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">Islamic conquest of most of the Iberian peninsula</a>. <i>Mons Calpe</i> was renamed <i>Jabal \xe1\xb9\xac\xc4\x81riq</i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic-language text">\xd8\xac\xd8\xa8\xd9\x84 \xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x82</span>), "the Mount of Tariq", subsequently corrupted into <i>Gibraltar</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hills-13_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hills-13-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1160 the <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohad</a> Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu&#39;min">Abd al-Mu\'min</a> ordered that a permanent settlement, including a castle, be built. It received the name of Medinat al-Fath (City of the Victory).<sup id="cite_ref-norris_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The Tower of Homage of the <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Castle" title="Moorish Castle">Moorish Castle</a> remains standing today.\n</p><p>From 1274 onwards, the town was fought over and captured by the <a href="/wiki/Nasrid_dynasty" title="Nasrid dynasty">Nasrids</a> of Granada (in 1237 and 1374), the <a href="/wiki/Marinids" class="mw-redirect" title="Marinids">Marinids</a> of Morocco (in 1274 and 1333) and the kings of <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a> (in 1309).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span></h3>\n<p>In 1462 Gibraltar was <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Siege_of_Gibraltar" class="mw-redirect" title="Eighth Siege of Gibraltar">captured</a> by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Alonso_de_Guzm%C3%A1n,_1st_Duke_of_Medina_Sidonia" title="Juan Alonso de Guzm\xc3\xa1n, 1st Duke of Medina Sidonia">Juan Alonso de Guzm\xc3\xa1n, 1st Duke of Medina Sidonia</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Granada" title="Emirate of Granada">Emirate of Granada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the conquest, <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_Castile" title="Henry IV of Castile">Henry IV of Castile</a> assumed the additional title of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Gibraltar" title="Kingdom of Gibraltar">King of Gibraltar</a>, establishing it as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarca</a></i> of the <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Gibraltar" title="Campo de Gibraltar">Campo Llano de Gibraltar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Six years later, Gibraltar was restored to the Duke of Medina Sidonia, who sold it in 1474 to a group of 4350 <i><a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">conversos</a></i> (Christian converts from Judaism) from <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="C\xc3\xb3rdoba, Spain">Cordova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seville,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Seville, Spain">Seville</a> and in exchange for maintaining the garrison of the town for two years, after which time they were expelled, returning to their home towns or moving on to other parts of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In 1501 Gibraltar passed back to the Spanish Crown, and <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Royal_warrant_(document)" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal warrant (document)">Royal Warrant</a> granting Gibraltar the coat of arms that it still uses.\n</p><p>In 1704, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, a combined <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Anglo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> fleet, representing the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(League_of_Augsburg)" title="Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)">Grand Alliance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">captured the town of Gibraltar</a> on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Archduke Charles of Austria</a> in his campaign to become King of Spain. Subsequently, most of the population left the town with many settling nearby.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> As the Alliance\'s campaign faltered, the 1713 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> was negotiated, which ceded control of Gibraltar to Britain to secure Britain\'s withdrawal from the war. Unsuccessful attempts by Spanish monarchs to regain Gibraltar were made with the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Gibraltar_(1727)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Gibraltar (1727)">siege of 1727</a> and again with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Gibraltar" title="Great Siege of Gibraltar">Great Siege of Gibraltar</a> (1779 to 1783), during the <a href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="American War of Independence">American War of Independence</a>.\n</p><p>After the destructive Great Siege, the town was almost entirely rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-At_an_architectural_crossroads_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-At_an_architectural_crossroads-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Giovanni Maria Boschetti, who arrived in Gibraltar in 1784 as a 25-year-old from Milan, where he is thought to have been a stonemason or engineer, built the Victualling Yard (completed in 1812) and many other buildings. Boschetti is regarded as having been responsible for setting the old town\'s style, described by Claire Montado, chief executive of the Gibraltar Heritage Trust, as "military-ordnance-style arched doorways, Italianate stucco relief, Genoese shutters, English Regency ironwork balconies, Spanish stained glass and Georgian sash and casement windows."<sup id="cite_ref-At_an_architectural_crossroads_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-At_an_architectural_crossroads-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Gibraltar became a key base for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> and played an important role leading up to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a> (21 October 1805). Its strategic location made it a key base during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1854\xe2\x80\x931856. In the 18th century, the peacetime military garrison fluctuated in numbers from a minimum of 1,100 to a maximum of 5,000. The first half of the 19th century saw a significant increase of population to more than 17,000 in 1860, as people from Britain and all around the Mediterranean \xe2\x80\x93 Italian, Portuguese, Maltese, Jewish and French \xe2\x80\x93 took up residence in the town.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Its strategic value increased with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>, as it lay on the sea route between the UK and the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> east of Suez. In the later 19th century, major investments were made to improve the fortifications and the port.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_history">Contemporary history</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Gibraltar_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Gibraltar during World War II">Military history of Gibraltar during World War II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_Brexit_on_Gibraltar" title="Effect of Brexit on Gibraltar">Effect of Brexit on Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar,_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/220px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/330px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/440px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2486" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar,_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shown here during the Second World War, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Dakota" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas Dakota">Douglas Dakota</a> of <a href="/wiki/BOAC" class="mw-redirect" title="BOAC">BOAC</a> is silhouetted at Gibraltar by the batteries of searchlights on the Rock, as crews prepare it for a night flight to the United Kingdom</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Gibraltar_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Gibraltar during World War II">During the Second World War</a>, most of Gibraltar\'s <a href="/wiki/Evacuation_of_the_Gibraltarian_civilian_population_during_World_War_II" title="Evacuation of the Gibraltarian civilian population during World War II">civilian population was evacuated</a>, mainly to London, but also to parts of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Camp">Gibraltar Camp</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>. The Rock was strengthened as a <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">fortress</a>. On 18 July 1940, the <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy French</a> <a href="/wiki/Vichy_French_Air_Force" title="Vichy French Air Force">air force</a> attacked Gibraltar in retaliation for the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Mers-el-K%C3%A9bir" title="Attack on Mers-el-K\xc3\xa9bir">British bombing</a> of the Vichy navy. The naval base and the ships based there played a key role in the provisioning and supply of the island of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> during <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">its long siege</a>. As well as frequent short runs, known as "Club Runs", towards Malta to fly off aircraft reinforcements (initially <a href="/wiki/Hawker_hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawker hurricane">Hurricanes</a>, but later, notably from the USN aircraft carrier <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(CV-7)" title="USS Wasp (CV-7)">Wasp</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Spitfires</a>), the critical <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pedestal" title="Operation Pedestal">Operation Pedestal</a> convoy was run from Gibraltar in August 1942. This resupplied the island at a critical time in the face of concentrated air attacks from German and Italian forces. Spanish dictator <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>\'s reluctance to allow the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">German Army</a> onto Spanish soil frustrated a German plan to capture the Rock, codenamed <a href="/wiki/Operation_Felix" title="Operation Felix">Operation Felix</a>.\n</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/250px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/375px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/500px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Buildings of the former <a href="/wiki/HM_Dockyard,_Gibraltar" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Dockyard, Gibraltar">HM Dockyard, Gibraltar</a>, dating from the 1895 expansion</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 1950s, Franco renewed Spain\'s claim to sovereignty over Gibraltar and restricted movement between Gibraltar and Spain. Gibraltarians voted overwhelmingly to remain under British sovereignty in the <a href="/wiki/1967_Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum" title="1967 Gibraltar sovereignty referendum">1967 Gibraltar sovereignty referendum</a>, which led to the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_1969" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 1969">Gibraltar Constitution Order</a> in 1969. In response, Spain completely closed the border with Gibraltar and severed all communication links.<sup id="cite_ref-Jordine2009_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jordine2009-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The border with Spain was partially reopened in 1982 and fully reopened in 1985 before Spain\'s accession to the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a>.\n</p><p>In the early 2000s, Britain and Spain were in negotiations over a potential agreement that would see them sharing sovereignty over Gibraltar. The government of Gibraltar organized a <a href="/wiki/2002_Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum" title="2002 Gibraltar sovereignty referendum">referendum</a> on the plan, and 99% of the population voted to reject it.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The British government committed to respecting the Gibraltarians\' wishes.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">new Constitution Order</a> was approved in referendum in 2006. A process of tripartite negotiations started in 2006 between Spain, Gibraltar and the UK, ending some restrictions and dealing with disputes in some specific areas such as air movements, customs procedures, telecommunications, pensions and cultural exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/British_referendum_on_membership_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="British referendum on membership of the European Union">British referendum on membership of the European Union</a> 96% of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarians_voted_to_remain" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltarians voted to remain">Gibraltarians voted to remain</a> on an 84% turnout.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Spain renewed calls for joint Spanish\xe2\x80\x93British control of the peninsula;<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> these were strongly rebuffed by Gibraltar\'s Chief Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On 18 October 2018, however, Spain seemed to have reached an agreement with the United Kingdom in relation to its objections to Gibraltar leaving the EU with the UK, with Spain\'s prime minister <a href="/wiki/Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Pedro S\xc3\xa1nchez">Pedro S\xc3\xa1nchez</a> stating, "Gibraltar will no longer be a problem in arriving at a Brexit deal."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 January 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">UK left the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_Brexit_on_Gibraltar" title="Effect of Brexit on Gibraltar">consequently</a> so did Gibraltar. Under the terms of the transition phase in the <a href="/wiki/Brexit_withdrawal_agreement" title="Brexit withdrawal agreement">Brexit withdrawal agreement</a>, Gibraltar\'s relationship with the EU continued unchanged until the end of 2020 when it was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/EU%E2%80%93UK_Trade_and_Cooperation_Agreement" title="EU\xe2\x80\x93UK Trade and Cooperation Agreement">EU\xe2\x80\x93UK Trade and Cooperation Agreement</a>. On 31 December 2020, the UK and Spain agreed in principle on a basis for the EU and the UK to negotiate an agreement through which Gibraltar would participate in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-GibStatement_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GibStatement-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> to avoid a hard border with Spain. The arrangements have not entered into force,<sup id="cite_ref-GibStatement_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GibStatement-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> but both sides aim to keep delays at the border at a minimum in the meantime.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Gibraltar" title="Politics of Gibraltar">Politics of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" class="mw-redirect" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">Disputed status of Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_development_in_modern_Gibraltar" title="Political development in modern Gibraltar">Political development in modern Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/220px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/330px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/440px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main Street entrance to the Governor\'s Residence, <a href="/wiki/The_Convent_(Gibraltar)" title="The Convent (Gibraltar)">The Convent</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Mackintosh_Square" title="John Mackintosh Square">John Mackintosh Square</a> entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">Gibraltar Parliament</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Under its current <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">constitution</a>, Gibraltar has almost complete internal <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">self-governance</a> through a <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">parliament</a><sup id="cite_ref-publications.parliament.uk_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-publications.parliament.uk-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> elected for a term of up to four years. The <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> parliament presently consists of 17 elected members, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_Gibraltar_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Speakers of the Gibraltar Parliament">Speaker</a> who is not elected, but appointed by a resolution of the parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gibraltar" title="Government of Gibraltar">government</a> consists of 10 elected members. The head of state is the British monarch <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, who is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Gibraltar" title="Governor of Gibraltar">Governor of Gibraltar</a>. The governor enacts day-to-day matters on the advice of the Gibraltar Parliament, but is responsible to the British government in respect of defence, foreign policy, internal security and general good governance.\nJudicial and other appointments are made on behalf of the monarch in consultation with the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gibraltar" title="Chief Minister of Gibraltar">head of the elected government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2011_Gibraltar_general_election" title="2011 Gibraltar general election">2011 election</a> was contested by the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Social_Democrats" title="Gibraltar Social Democrats">Gibraltar Social Democrats</a> (GSD), <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Socialist_Labour_Party" title="Gibraltar Socialist Labour Party">Gibraltar Socialist Labour Party</a> (GSLP)-<a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Gibraltar" title="Liberal Party of Gibraltar">Liberal Party of Gibraltar</a> (LPG) Alliance and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democratic_Party_(Gibraltar)" title="Progressive Democratic Party (Gibraltar)">Progressive Democratic Party</a> (PDP). The PDP was a new party, formed in 2006 and fielded candidates in the 2007 election, but none were elected. The head of government is the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gibraltar" title="Chief Minister of Gibraltar">Chief Minister</a> (as of December&#160;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Picardo" title="Fabian Picardo">Fabian Picardo</a>). All local political parties oppose any transfer of sovereignty to Spain, instead supporting <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>. The main UK opposition parties also support this policy, and it is British government policy not to engage in talks about the sovereignty of Gibraltar without the consent of the people of Gibraltar.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar was part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, having joined through the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities_Act_1972_(UK)" title="European Communities Act 1972 (UK)">European Communities Act 1972 (UK)</a>, which gave effect to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_1972" title="Treaty of Accession 1972">Treaty of Accession 1972</a>, as a dependent territory of the United Kingdom under what was then article 227(4) of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_Establishing_the_European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty Establishing the European Community">Treaty Establishing the European Community</a> covering <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar and the European Union">special member state territories</a>, with exemption from some areas such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. It is the only <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British Overseas Territory">British Overseas Territory</a> which was part of the European Union. After a 10-year campaign for the right to vote in <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in the European Union">European elections</a>, from 2004 to 2019 the people of Gibraltar participated in elections for the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England constituency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> On 23 June 2016 Gibraltar voted along with the United Kingdom in the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">EU referendum</a>; 96% of its population voted to remain, but the overall United Kingdom result gave a 51.9% majority to leaving the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, Spanish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro S\xc3\xa1nchez (politician)">Pedro S\xc3\xa1nchez</a> stated on 18 October 2018 that the Gibraltar protocol had been "resolved" and that Spain will hold no objection when Gibraltar leaves the EU with Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar was nominated to be included on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories</a> by the United Kingdom when the list was created in 1946<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and has been listed ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The government of Gibraltar has actively worked to have Gibraltar removed from the list,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and in 2008 the British government declared Gibraltar\'s continued presence on the list an anachronism.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> in its own right and is represented by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> but was granted Associate Membership of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Foundation" title="Commonwealth Foundation">Commonwealth Foundation</a> in 2004. Gibraltar has competed in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> since 1958.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2">Party\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">Members of Parliament</a>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="1" style="width: 2px; background-color: Labour Party">Socialist Labour</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="1" style="width: 2px; background-color: #0A5BA6;" data-sort-value="Gibraltar Social scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Gibraltar" title="Liberal Party of Gibraltar">Liberal</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="1" style="width: 2px; background-color: #EC6927;" data-sort-value="Together Gibraltar">\n</td>\n<td rowspan="1" style="text-align: left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Together_Gibraltar" title="Together Gibraltar"><span class="nowrap">Together Gibraltar</span></a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Total\n</th>\n<th>17\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">Bay of Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Artificial_Reef" title="Gibraltar Artificial Reef">Gibraltar Artificial Reef</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/220px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/330px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/440px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the Rock of Gibraltar from the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Steps" title="Mediterranean Steps">Mediterranean Steps</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar2021OSM.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Gibraltar2021OSM.png/220px-Gibraltar2021OSM.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Gibraltar2021OSM.png/330px-Gibraltar2021OSM.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Gibraltar2021OSM.png/440px-Gibraltar2021OSM.png 2x" data-file-width="2789" data-file-height="3447" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar2021OSM.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Enlargeable, detailed map of Gibraltar</div></div></div>\n<p>Gibraltar\'s territory covers 6.7 square kilometres (2.6&#160;sq&#160;mi) and shares a 1.2-kilometre (0.75&#160;mi) land border with Spain. The town of <a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La L\xc3\xadnea de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n">La L\xc3\xadnea de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_C%C3%A1diz" title="List of municipalities in C\xc3\xa1diz">municipality</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Province of C\xc3\xa1diz">province of C\xc3\xa1diz</a>, lies on the Spanish side of the border. The Spanish hinterland forms the <a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarca</a> of <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Gibraltar" title="Campo de Gibraltar">Campo de Gibraltar</a> (literally "Countryside of Gibraltar"). The shoreline measures 12 kilometres (7.5&#160;mi) in length. There are two coasts ("Sides") of Gibraltar: the East Side, which contains the settlements of <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Bay,_Gibraltar" title="Sandy Bay, Gibraltar">Sandy Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Bay" title="Catalan Bay">Catalan Bay</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Westside_(Gibraltar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westside (Gibraltar)">Westside</a>, where the vast majority of the population lives. Gibraltar has no administrative divisions but is divided into seven <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Major_Residential_Areas" title="Gibraltar Major Residential Areas">Major Residential Areas</a>.\n</p><p>Having negligible <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> and few natural <a href="/wiki/Freshwater" class="mw-redirect" title="Freshwater">freshwater</a> resources, limited to natural wells in the north, until recently Gibraltar used large concrete or natural rock <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">water catchments</a> to collect rainwater. Fresh water from the boreholes is nowadays supplemented by two <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">desalination</a> plants: a <a href="/wiki/Reverse_osmosis" title="Reverse osmosis">reverse osmosis</a> plant, constructed in a tunnel within the rock, and a <a href="/wiki/Multi-stage_flash_distillation" title="Multi-stage flash distillation">multi-stage flash distillation</a> plant at North Mole.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar\'s terrain consists of the 426-metre-high (1,398&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> made of <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, and the narrow coastal lowland surrounding it. It contains many tunnelled roads, most of which are still operated by the military and closed to the general public.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg" class="image" title="Morocco (top far left across Strait); Spain: Algeciras (top centre across Bay of Gibraltar) and La Linea (right); Gibraltar cruise port and airport runway (right foreground); from the Rock"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg/1000px-View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg/1500px-View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg/2000px-View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7966" data-file-height="1312" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg" title="File:View from top of Gib rock.jpg"> </a></div>Morocco (top far left across Strait); Spain: Algeciras (top centre across Bay of Gibraltar) and La Linea (right); Gibraltar cruise port and airport runway (right foreground); from the Rock</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Gibraltar" title="Climate of Gibraltar">Climate of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<p>Gibraltar has a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a> <i>Csa</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> with mild, rainy winters and warm, dry summers. As is the case for nearby <a href="/wiki/Algeciras" title="Algeciras">Algeciras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarifa" title="Tarifa">Tarifa</a>, summers are significantly cooler and annual temperature more constant than other cities on the southern coast of the Iberian peninsula because of its position on the Strait of Gibraltar. Rain occurs mainly in winter, with summer being generally dry. Its average annual temperature is about 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F) as a daily high and 15&#160;\xc2\xb0C (59&#160;\xc2\xb0F) as the overnight low. In the coldest month, January, the high temperature averages 16.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and the overnight low is 11&#160;\xc2\xb0C (52&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and the average sea temperature is 16&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61&#160;\xc2\xb0F). In the warmest month, August, the daily high temperature is 25&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77&#160;\xc2\xb0F), the overnight low is 20&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and the average sea temperature is 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-DWD_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DWD-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n<sup id="cite_ref-weather2travel_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather2travel-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em;
