role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Gibraltar" title="List of mammals of Gibraltar">List of mammals of Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Gibraltar" title="List of birds of Gibraltar">List of birds of Gibraltar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_and_reptiles_of_Gibraltar" title="List of amphibians and reptiles of Gibraltar">List of amphibians and reptiles of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/220px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/330px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/440px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1088" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Iberis_gibraltarica" title="Iberis gibraltarica">Gibraltar candytuft</a> growing at the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Botanic_Gardens" title="Gibraltar Botanic Gardens">Gibraltar Botanic Gardens</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/220px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/330px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/440px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png 2x" data-file-width="789" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">common dolphin</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">Bay of Gibraltar</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Over 500 different species of <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> grow on the Rock. Gibraltar is the only place in Europe where the <i>Gibraltar candytuft</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Iberis_gibraltarica" title="Iberis gibraltarica">Iberis gibraltarica</a></i>) is found growing in the wild; the plant is otherwise native to North Africa. It is the symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar#Upper_Rock_Nature_Reserve" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Upper Rock nature reserve</a>. <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">Olive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a> trees are among the most common of those growing around the Rock.\n</p><p>Most of the Rock\'s upper area is covered by a <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserve</a> which is home to around 230 <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Barbary_macaques" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Barbary macaques">Barbary macaques</a>, the famous "apes" of Gibraltar, which are actually <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">monkeys</a>. These are the only wild apes or monkeys found in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> This species, known scientifically as <i><a href="/wiki/Macaca_sylvanus" class="mw-redirect" title="Macaca sylvanus">Macaca sylvanus</a></i>, is listed as endangered by the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> and is declining. Three-quarters of the world population live in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Atlas" title="Middle Atlas">Middle Atlas</a> mountains of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. Recent genetic studies and historical documents point to their presence on the Rock before its <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">capture by the British</a>, having possibly been introduced during the Islamic period. A superstition analogous to that of the <a href="/wiki/Raven" title="Raven">ravens</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> states that if the apes ever leave, so will the British. In 1944, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> was so concerned about the dwindling population of apes that he sent a message to the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_(British_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Secretary (British Empire)">Colonial Secretary</a> requesting that something be done about the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other mammals found in Gibraltar include rabbits, foxes and bats. Dolphins and whales are frequently seen in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">Bay of Gibraltar</a>. Migrating birds are very common and Gibraltar is home to the only <a href="/wiki/Barbary_partridge" title="Barbary partridge">Barbary partridges</a> found on the European continent.\n</p><p>In 1991, Graham Watson, Gibraltar\'s <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEP</a>, highlighted <a href="/wiki/Conservationism" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservationism">conservationists</a>\' fears that <a href="/wiki/Urban_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban development">urban development</a>, tourism and <a href="/wiki/Invasive_plant_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasive plant species">invasive plant species</a> were threatening Gibraltar\'s own plants as well as birds and <a href="/wiki/Bat_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Bat species">bat species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RockofGibraltar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/RockofGibraltar.jpg/220px-RockofGibraltar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/RockofGibraltar.jpg/330px-RockofGibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/RockofGibraltar.jpg/440px-RockofGibraltar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3903" data-file-height="2883" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RockofGibraltar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Rock of Gibraltar (2010)</div></div></div>\n<p>In May 2016 a report by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> showed that Gibraltar had the worst air quality in any British territory. The report concentrated on <a href="/wiki/PM10" class="mw-redirect" title="PM10">PM10</a> and <a href="/wiki/PM2.5" class="mw-redirect" title="PM2.5">PM2.5</a> pollutants in the air.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Gibraltar" title="Economy of Gibraltar">Economy of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/170px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/255px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/340px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg 2x" data-file-width="666" data-file-height="998" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The semi-wild <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Barbary_macaques" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Barbary macaques">Barbary macaques</a> are an integral feature in <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Gibraltar" title="Tourism in Gibraltar">Gibraltar\'s tourism</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">British military</a> traditionally dominated <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Gibraltar" title="Economy of Gibraltar">Gibraltar\'s economy</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Naval_dockyard" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval dockyard">naval dockyard</a> providing the bulk of economic activity. This, however, has diminished over the last 20 years and is estimated to account for only 7 per cent of the local economy, compared to over 60 per cent in 1984. Today, Gibraltar\'s economy is dominated by four main sectors: <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">financial services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Online_gambling" title="Online gambling">online gambling</a>, shipping, and tourism, which includes duty-free retail sales to visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The territory also has a small manufacturing sector, with one company (Bassadone Automotive Group) supplying ambulances and other project vehicles converted locally from <a href="/wiki/SUV" class="mw-redirect" title="SUV">SUV</a> vehicles to the United Nations and other agencies, employing some 320 staff across its range of activities.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar\'s <a href="/wiki/Labour_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour market">labour market</a> shows an extremely low unemployment rate of around 1 per cent. Nearly half (46%) of the total employment is covered by frontier workers (employees who are normally resident in Spain but are employed in Gibraltar), the large majority of them (59%) of Spanish nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early 2000s, many <a href="/wiki/Bookmaker" title="Bookmaker">bookmakers</a> and online gaming operators moved to Gibraltar to benefit from operating in a regulated jurisdiction with a favourable <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">corporate tax</a> regime. This corporate tax regime for non-resident controlled companies was phased out by January 2011 and replaced by a still favourable fixed corporate tax rate of 10 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tourism is also a significant industry. Gibraltar is a popular port for cruise ships and attracts day visitors from resorts in Spain. The Rock is a popular tourist attraction, particularly among British tourists and residents in the southern coast of Spain. It is also a popular shopping destination, and all goods and services are <a href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Value added tax">VAT</a> free, but may be subject to Gibraltar taxes. Many of the large British high street chains have branches or franchises in Gibraltar including <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marks_%26_Spencer" title="Marks &amp; Spencer">Marks &amp; Spencer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mothercare" title="Mothercare">Mothercare</a>. Branches and franchises of international retailers such as <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hilfiger" title="Tommy Hilfiger">Tommy Hilfiger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunglass_Hut_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunglass Hut International">Sunglass Hut</a> are also present in Gibraltar, as is the Spanish clothing company <a href="/wiki/Mango_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mango (clothing)">Mango</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queensway Quay Marina, along with <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Village,_Gibraltar" title="Ocean Village, Gibraltar">Ocean Village</a>, are two exclusive residential districts.</div></div></div>\n<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_banks_in_Gibraltar" title="List of banks in Gibraltar">British and international banks</a> have operations based in Gibraltar. <a href="/wiki/Jyske_Bank" title="Jyske Bank">Jyske Bank</a> claims to be the oldest bank in the country, based on Jyske\'s acquisition in 1987 of <a href="/wiki/Banco_Galliano" title="Banco Galliano">Banco Galliano</a>, which began operations in Gibraltar in 1855. An ancestor of <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">Barclays</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Bank" title="Anglo-Egyptian Bank">Anglo-Egyptian Bank</a>, entered in 1888, and Credit Foncier (now <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A9dit_Agricole" title="Cr\xc3\xa9dit Agricole">Cr\xc3\xa9dit Agricole</a>) entered in 1920.\n</p><p>In 1967, Gibraltar enacted the Companies (Taxation and Concessions) Ordinance (now an Act), which provided for special tax treatment for international business.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> This was one of the factors leading to the growth of professional services such as <a href="/wiki/Private_banking" title="Private banking">private banking</a> and captive insurance management. Gibraltar has several attractive attributes as a <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a>, including a <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Gibraltar" title="Law of Gibraltar">legal system</a> and access to the EU single market in financial services. The Financial Services Commission (FSC),<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> which was established by an ordinance in 1989 (now an Act) that took effect in 1991, regulates the finance sector.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, the Department of Trade and Industry established its Gibraltar Finance Centre (GFC) Division to facilitate the development the <a href="/wiki/Financial_sector_development" title="Financial sector development">financial sector development</a>. As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Gibraltar has 0.103 <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(audit_firms)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Four (audit firms)">Big Four</a> accounting firm offices per 1,000 population, the second highest in the world after the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, and 0.6 banks per 1,000 people, the fifth most banks per capita in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there is <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_Brexit_on_Gibraltar" title="Effect of Brexit on Gibraltar">very significant uncertainty</a> on continuing access to the EU single market after the forthcoming <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The currency of Gibraltar is the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_pound" title="Gibraltar pound">Gibraltar pound</a>, issued by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gibraltar" title="Government of Gibraltar">Government of Gibraltar</a> under the terms of the 1934 <i>Currency Notes Act</i>. These banknotes are <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a> in Gibraltar alongside Bank of England banknotes.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-currnotesact_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currnotesact-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In a <a href="/wiki/Currency_board" title="Currency board">currency board</a> arrangement, these notes are issued against reserves of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">sterling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-currnotesact_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currnotesact-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Clearing and settlement of funds is conducted in sterling.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coins_of_the_Gibraltar_pound" class="mw-redirect" title="Coins of the Gibraltar pound">Coins</a> in circulation follow British denominations but have separate designs. Unofficially, most retail outlets in Gibraltar accept the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, though some <a href="/wiki/Payphone" title="Payphone">payphones</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Post_Office" title="Royal Gibraltar Post Office">Royal Gibraltar Post Office</a>, along with all other government offices, do not.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Gibraltar" title="Demographics of Gibraltar">Demographics of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/220px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/330px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/440px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned" title="Cathedral of St. Mary the Crowned">Cathedral of St. Mary the Crowned</a> was built in 1462 and is the territory\'s oldest Catholic church.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/220px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/330px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/440px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4352" data-file-height="2904" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple" title="Gibraltar Hindu Temple">Gibraltar Hindu Temple</a> opened in 2000.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim_Mosque" title="Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim Mosque">Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim Mosque</a> was a gift from <a href="/wiki/Fahd_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Fahd of Saudi Arabia">King Fahd</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Gibraltar is one of the most densely populated territories in the world, with a usually-resident population in 2012 of 32,194<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> equivalent to approximately 4,959 inhabitants per square kilometre (12,840/sq&#160;mi). The growing demand for space is being increasingly met by <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>; reclaimed land makes up approximately one-tenth of the territory\'s total area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltarian people">Gibraltarian people</a></div>\n<p>The demographics of Gibraltar reflect the many <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Economic_migrant" title="Economic migrant">economic migrants</a> who came to the Rock over 300 years ago, after almost all of the Spanish population left in 1704.\n</p><p>Origin of surnames in the electoral roll by percentage is: British (27%), Spanish (26%, mostly <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusian</a> but also some 2% <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorcan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> (15%), <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> (15%), and <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">Maltese</a> (8%). There are also small (less than 1%) populations of other groups such as <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan people">Moroccans</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish people">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish people">Danish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">\n<caption><b> Usually-Resident Population and Persons Present in Gibraltar</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Resident Census\n</th>\n<th data-sort-type="number">1981<sup id="cite_ref-gibraltar.gov.gi_3-1"
